A Randomized, Double-Blind, Placebo-Controlled, 
Multi-Center Phase 3 Study of Denosumab on 
Prolonging Bone Metastasis-Free Survival in Men with 
Hormone-Refractory Prostate Cancer
3 
Prolonging bone metastasis-free survival in men with 
hormone-refractory (androgen independent) prostate 
cancer
To compare the treatment effect of denosumab with 
placebo on prolonging bone metastasis-free survival in 
men with hormone refractory (androgen independent) 
prostate cancer who have no bone metastasis at 
baseline.  
To compare the treatment effect of denosumab with 
placebo on:
(cid:120)
(cid:120)
To assess the safety and tolerability of denosumab 
compared with placebo
To evaluate the treatment effect of denosumab 
compared with placebo on the:
(cid:120)
(cid:120)
(cid:120)
(cid:120)
(cid:120)  prostate cancer progression at any site 
(cid:120)  prostate cancer progression-free survival
To assess serum trough levels of denosumab.
The overall risk of developing bone metastasis or death 
for the denosumab treated group is less than that of the 
placebo treated group.  It is anticipated that the true 
hazard ratio of denosumab compared with placebo will 
be 0.8. 
This is an international, phase 3, randomized, 
double-blind, placebo-controlled study in subjects with 
hormone refractory (androgen independent) prostate 
cancer.  Approximately 1400 subjects will be randomized 
in a 1:1 ratio to receive denosumab, 120 mg or placebo 
every 4 weeks (Q4W).  The randomization schedule will 
be stratified based on PSA criteria (PSA level 
(cid:116) 8.0 ng/mL AND PSA doubling time (cid:100) 10.0 months 
[yes/no]) and previous or current chemotherapy for 

fracture
change in prostate specific antigen (PSA) level
change in patient reported outcomes (PRO)
change in bone turnover markers

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:49)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:69)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:19)(cid:24)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:26)(cid:3)(cid:177)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:88)(cid:83)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:23)(cid:3)
(cid:39)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:88)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:23)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:28)(cid:23)(cid:3)

prostate cancer (yes/no). 
Subjects enrolled on the study will receive investigational 
product Q4W until approximately 660 subjects have 
developed bone metastasis or died and the primary 
efficacy and safety analysis is completed.
If denosumab is determined to have a positive 
benefit:risk profile compared with placebo, all subjects 
currently undergoing every 4 weeks scheduled 
assessments will be offered open-label denosumab at a 
dose of 120 mg SC until subjects have developed a 
bone metastasis, access to commercially available 
product in this setting, or for up to 3 years, whichever
comes first.  If the benefit:risk profile is not positive, all 
subjects will be followed for survival for 3 years after the 
last dose of blinded investigational product (IP). 
It is strongly recommended that all subjects receive daily 
supplements of at least 500 mg of calcium and at least 
400 IU of vitamin D.  
A data monitoring committee (DMC) will review safety 
and efficacy data at regular intervals during the blinded 
treatment phase.

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:71)(cid:88)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:69)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:36)(cid:48)(cid:42)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:25)(cid:21)(cid:12)(cid:3)

this setting, or for up to 3 years, whichever comes first.  
If the benefit:risk profile is not positive, all subjects will be

Placebo will be used as the control group in this study.  
(cid:37)(cid:79)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:55)(cid:85)(cid:72)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:51)(cid:75)(cid:68)(cid:86)(cid:72)
Informed consent must be obtained before any study 
specific procedures are performed.  
Upon meeting all eligibility criteria and completing all 
screening assessments, subjects will be randomized in a 
stratified manner to 1 of 2 treatment groups (denosumab 
or placebo) within 8 days before the first administration 
of investigational product (study day 1).  Subjects will 
receive investigational product Q4W until approximately 
660 subjects have developed bone metastasis or died.  
The following assessments will be performed at various 
visits throughout the study:  medical and medication 
history, ECOG performance status, height (at screening 
only), weight, and physical examination with vital signs 
(temperature, pulse, blood pressure, respiratory rate), 
radioisotope bone scans, skeletal survey (x-rays), oral 
examination, hematology, serum chemistry, denosumab 
antibody assay, denosumab level, urine collection, PSA, 
testosterone, PRO assessments. 
Adverse events and concomitant medications will be 
recorded.  
Subjects who withdraw early from investigational product 
administration will continue on study, without 
investigational product administration, according to the 
Schedule of Assessments (
(cid:50)(cid:83)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:16)(cid:47)(cid:68)(cid:69)(cid:72)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:55)(cid:85)(cid:72)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:51)(cid:75)(cid:68)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:3)
Informed consent must be obtained before participation 
in the open-label treatment phase.  
The following procedures will be performed at various 
visits throughout the open-label treatment phase:  ECOG 
performance status; oral examinations; serum chemistry; 
and serum for anti-denosumab antibody assay.
Adverse events and concomitant medications will be 
recorded throughout the open-label treatment phase.(cid:3)
(cid:54)(cid:88)(cid:85)(cid:89)(cid:76)(cid:89)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:79)(cid:82)(cid:90)(cid:16)(cid:88)(cid:83)
For subjects ending study participation before the 
open-label treatment phase or ending treatment during 
the open-label treatment phase, follow up survival data 
will be collected by clinic visit or telephone contact every 
6 months for up to 3 years after the last dose of blinded 
investigational product.

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:71)(cid:88)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:69)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:36)(cid:48)(cid:42)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:25)(cid:21)(cid:12)(cid:3)
(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:49)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:69)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:19)(cid:24)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:26)(cid:3)(cid:177)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:88)(cid:83)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:23)(cid:3)
(cid:39)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:88)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:27)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:28)(cid:23)(cid:3)

(cid:54)(cid:87)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:86)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:70)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:38)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:86)(cid:76)(cid:71)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:86)(cid:3) This study is designed to compare the treatment effect of 

denosumab with placebo on prolonging bone 
metastasis-free survival in men with hormone refractory 
(androgen independent) prostate cancer who have no 
bone metastasis at baseline. 
Approximately 1400 subjects will be randomized in a 
1:1 ratio to receive denosumab or placebo.  The 
randomization schedule will be stratified based on PSA 
criteria (PSA level (cid:116) 8.0 ng/mL AND PSA doubling time 
(cid:100) 10.0 months [yes/no]) and previous or current 
chemotherapy for prostate cancer (yes/no).  A planned 
interim analysis will be conducted when approximately 
330 events of bone metastasis or death have occurred.  
The treatment period will end after approximately 
660 subjects have developed bone metastasis or died 
and the final analysis will be conducted.  
The primary efficacy endpoint, bone metastasis-free 
survival, will be analyzed using a Cox proportional 
hazard model (Cox, 1972) with treatment groups as the 
independent variable and stratified by the randomization 
stratification factors.  If denosumab is determined to be 
superior to placebo with respect to the primary efficacy 
endpoint, the secondary efficacy endpoint time to first 
bone metastasis (either symptomatic or asymptomatic) 
excluding deaths will be tested.  If denosumab is further 
determined to be superior to placebo with respect to time 
to first bone metastasis (either symptomatic or 
asymptomatic) excluding deaths, the secondary efficacy 
endpoint overall survival time will be tested. 
Safety will be characterized by evaluated incidence and 
severity of adverse events, and toxicity grade shift in lab 
values.  The number and percentage of patients who 
develop neutralizing anti-denosumab antibodies will be
tabulated by study visit.  
Amgen Inc

Study Term
Date of Randomization

Definition
date subject is randomized; enrollment date

Study Day 1

Denosumab

End of Study

first day investigational product is administered

formally known as AMG 162, monoclonal antibody to RANKL; 
investigational product
If the benefit:risk is positive, the end of study is defined as 4 weeks 
after the last dose of denosumab in the open-label treatment phase.  
If the benefit:risk is not positive, the end of study is defined as 4
weeks after the last dose of investigational product in the end of the 
blinded treatment phase

End of Treatment

date of the last administration of investigational product

Enrollment Date

date of randomization

Screening Period

Primary Analysis Data 
Cut-off Date

time from when the subject signs the informed consent until 
randomization
Anticipated date on which 660 subjects will develop bone metastasis 
or die

(cid:37)(cid:36)(cid:38)(cid:46)(cid:42)(cid:53)(cid:50)(cid:56)(cid:49)(cid:39)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:49)(cid:39)(cid:3)(cid:53)(cid:36)(cid:55)(cid:44)(cid:50)(cid:49)(cid:36)(cid:47)(cid:40)(cid:3)

(cid:39)(cid:76)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:68)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:3)

Bone metastases are a frequent finding in patients with advanced prostate cancer and 
the complications (skeletal related events, SRE) associated with them confer a 
significant disease and health-economic burden (Reed et al, 2004).  In contrast to 
treatment of established bone metastases (Zometa(cid:163) prescribing information, 2005), no
medication is approved specifically for the prevention of bone metastases in prostate 
cancer.  The current standard of care is to observe patients until macroscopic disease in 
the bone is observed, which then can be treated with the bisphosphonate zoledronic 
acid (Zometa(cid:163)) to prevent SREs. 

(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:71)(cid:88)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:69)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:36)(cid:48)(cid:42)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:25)(cid:21)(cid:12)(cid:3)
(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:49)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:69)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:19)(cid:24)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:26)(cid:3)(cid:177)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:88)(cid:83)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:23)(cid:3)
(cid:39)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:88)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:27)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:28)(cid:23)(cid:3)

Patients with advanced prostate cancer who fail to respond to hormonal therapies but 
have no detectable bone metastases are at risk of developing clinically apparent bone 
metastatic disease (Smith et al, 2005).  The risk for developing bone metastases is even 
higher in those androgen-refractory patients who present with either high baseline PSA 
and/or aggressive PSA-kinetics as evidenced from short PSA doubling times 
(Smith et al , 2005).  Such a high-risk patient population has been chosen for this 
protocol.  These patients could benefit from new therapeutic approaches, which would 
either prevent bone metastases completely or would delay their occurrence.  Thus, a 
high unmet medical need exists for effective therapy in that indication. 

The biologic hallmark of bone metastases, irrespective of their osteoblastic or osteolytic 
radiographic appearance is increased osteoclastic activity (Body et al, 2003; 
Roodman, 2004; Yonou et al, 2004).  This activity can be demonstrated by both 
histological analysis of bone metastases as well as analysis of serum bone resorption 
markers (Percival et al, 1987; Demers et al, 2003).  On a molecular level, stimulation of 
the RANKL-RANK system has been identified as a main driver for increased osteoclastic 
activity (Teitelbaum & Ross, 2003), resulting in significant skeletal morbidity (SRE) in 
patients with bone metastases (Kong et al, 1999; Hofbauer et al, 2001), including those 
from prostate cancer (Brown et al, 2001; Brown et al, 2004; Lynch et al, 2005). 

A number of generally accepted concepts and preclinical observations support the 
hypothesis that inhibition of RANKL at a timepoint prior to the development of clinically 
detectable bone metastases in prostate cancer may delay their occurrence.  The 
mutually supportive interplay between locally increased osteoclastic activity and tumor 
cell proliferation (vicious cycle; [Guise, 2002]) may not only facilitate progression of 
established bone metastases, but may also facilitate earlier steps in their development 
(Roodman, 2004).  The hypothesis that increased osteoclastic bone resorption (eg, 
prostate cancer patients receiving androgen deprivation therapy; 
Michaelson et al., 2004) facilitates the development of bone metastases has already 
been demonstrated in preclinical models (Manishen et al., 1986; Kostenuik et al., 2004;
Padalecki et al., 2003; Chung et al, 2005).  It is therefore possible that inhibition of 
osteoclastic bone resorption by denosumab will render the bone microenvironment less 
fertile for the development of bone metastases, thus prolonging bone metastasis free 
survival in the target population of this protocol.

(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:71)(cid:88)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:69)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:36)(cid:48)(cid:42)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:25)(cid:21)(cid:12)(cid:3)
(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:49)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:69)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:19)(cid:24)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:26)(cid:3)(cid:177)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:88)(cid:83)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:23)(cid:3)
(cid:39)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:88)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:28)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:28)(cid:23)(cid:3)

(cid:21)(cid:17)(cid:21)(cid:3)

(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:69) (cid:37)(cid:68)(cid:70)(cid:78)(cid:74)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:88)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:3)

Perturbations in the balance between bone formation and resorption can lead to 
generalized osteoporosis (resulting from estrogen deficiency and aging) or local bone 
lysis (resulting from rheumatoid arthritis and bone metastases).  RANK-RANK ligand 
(RANKL) system has been identified as an essential mediator of osteoclast formation, 
function, and survival (Teitelbaum et al, 2003).  RANKL binds RANK on osteoclasts or 
osteoclast precursors to stimulate or promote differentiation into osteoclasts and activate 
mature osteoclasts to resorb bone.  Therefore, RANKL is a therapeutic target for 
diseases associated with increased bone resorption.

Denosumab is a fully human monoclonal IgG2 antibody to RANKL that binds with high 
affinity (Kd 3 x 10-12 M) and specificity to the soluble and cell membrane-bound forms of 
human RANKL.  Denosumab is highly specific because it binds only to RANKL and not 
to other members of the tumor necrosis factor (TNF) family, including TNF(cid:68), TNF(cid:69),
TNF-related apoptosis-inducing ligand, or CD40 ligand (Elliott et al, 2006).  Denosumab 
binding prevents the activation of RANK and inhibits the formation, activation, and
survival of osteoclasts.  As a consequence, bone resorption and cancer-induced bone 
destruction are reduced.  

Refer to the latest version of the Investigator’s brochure for additional and updated 
information on denosumab background, clinical experience, and safety information.

(cid:21)(cid:17)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:53)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:72)(cid:3)

The clinical rationale to study denosumab for the prolongation of bone metastasis free 
survival in high risk hormone-refractory (androgen independent) prostate cancer patients 
has been outlined above in Section 1.1.  The following is to provide a rationale for the 
chosen dose and regimen, which is based on the pharmacokinetic and 
pharmacodynamic (bone resorption marker inhibition) properties of denosumab.

Biochemical evidence of bone resorption has been shown to correlate with clinical 
complications in patients with established bone metastases  (Brown et al, 2005,
Coleman et al, 2005), and is an accepted tool to assist in dose selection in studies of 
antiresorptive agents.  Determination of bone turnover markers during antiresorptive 
therapy for the treatment of bone metastases enables a rapid determination of efficacy 
over a time period of 1 to 3 months (Berenson et al, 2001 a and b). 

(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:71)(cid:88)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:69)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:36)(cid:48)(cid:42)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:25)(cid:21)(cid:12)(cid:3)
(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:49)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:69)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:19)(cid:24)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:26)(cid:3)(cid:177)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:88)(cid:83)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:23)(cid:3)
(cid:39)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:88)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:28)(cid:23)(cid:3)

For the prevention of bone metastases in patients at high risk the dosing principles for 
patients with established disease apply based on the likelihood that prevention of bone 
metastases in effect is treatment of bone micrometastases.  It is not surprising that the 
published literature on prevention trials for bone metastases exclusively reports 
treatment doses/schedules of bisphosphonates in respective studies (see Table 1).

The results from Table 1 in their entirety suggest efficacy of high-dose antiresorptive 
treatment (oral clodronate) for the prevention of bone metastases in breast cancer.  High 
oral daily doses of 1600 mg clodronate are approved in Europe for the treatment of 
osteolytic lesions in patients with breast cancer or multiple myeloma.  The negative 
study results in prostate cancer reported by Mason et al (2004) cannot be extrapolated 
to the study planned by Amgen Inc, since the patient population to be recruited for the 
planned Amgen Inc trial is far more advanced and at higher risk of developing bone 
metastases, thus potentially revealing treatment effects not detectable in the less 
advanced patient population. 

Denosumab has been found to be pharmacodynamically effective and without clinical  
safety signals in doses up to 180 mg SC, Q4W for the treatment of established bone 
metastases.  Although bone micrometastases may constitute a lower tumor burden than 
radiographically detectable bone metastases, the microenvironmental milieu and the 
local interactions between tumor cells and osteoclasts can be expected to be 
comparable, and to require similar therapeutic drug concentrations.  This applies in

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:71)(cid:88)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:69)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:36)(cid:48)(cid:42)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:25)(cid:21)(cid:12)(cid:3)
(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:49)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:69)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:19)(cid:24)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:26)(cid:3)(cid:177)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:88)(cid:83)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:23)(cid:3)
(cid:39)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:88)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:20)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:28)(cid:23)(cid:3)

particular to the study population targeted in this study, because these patients are at 
high risk of developing bone metastases based on their baseline PSA characteristics 
(PSA (cid:116) 8.0 ng/mL and/or PSA doubling time (cid:100) 10.0 months). Amgen Inc therefore
considers the dose and schedule for the phase 3 studies for established bone 
metastases to be appropriate for the planned study in high risk patients with 
hormone-refractory (androgen independent) prostate cancer.

The dose and schedule selected for this study is denosumab 120 mg, SC, Q4W.

(cid:39)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:72)(cid:79)(cid:72)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:3)(cid:53)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:72)(cid:3)

The selection of the dose and schedule was based on safety, pharmacokinetic and 
pharmacodynamic data obtained from phase 1 and 2 studies described above.
Specifically, study 20040113 tested 5 different doses and schedules of SC denosumab 
versus IV bisphosphonates in 255 patients with breast cancer and bone metastases.  
Study 20040113 provided a comprehensive dataset guiding the dose selection for 
patients with bone metastases.  All 5 denosumab arms showed biological activity in 
reducing bone resorption which was comparable to that seen with bisphosphonates.
The rate of skeletal related events in the denosumab arms was not higher than that 
observed in the bisphosphonate arm.  Out of the denosumab doses and schedules 
tested, the regimen of 120 mg, Q4W was associated with maximum reduction of the 
bone turnover marker uNTX by week 13, the primary endpoint of that study. 

Unlike lower doses, the 120 mg, Q4W schedule avoided low exposure which could 
potentially translate into insufficient efficacy in some patients.  Denosumab was found to 
be safe and well tolerated in all study arms.  While no symptomatic hypocalcemia was 
recorded, the 120 mg, Q4W schedule (n = 41) appeared preferable because no grade 2
or higher hypocalcemia was recorded as opposed to 5 grade 2 and one grade 3
hypocalcemia in the denosumab 180 mg, Q4W group (n = 43).  Based on the favorable 
efficacy, safety and pharmacokinetic profile of that regimen observed in study 20040113, 
the 120 mg, Q4W schedule was chosen to be proceeded into phase 3 in patients with 
bone metastases.  For the prevention of bone metastases in patients at high risk the 
dosing principles for patients with established disease apply.  Therefore, the 120 mg, 
Q4W schedule was chosen for study 20050147 as well.

(cid:3)

(cid:39)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:88)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:28)(cid:23)(cid:3)

(cid:43)(cid:92)(cid:83)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:75)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:76)(cid:86)(cid:3)

The overall risk of developing bone metastasis or death for the denosumab treated 
group is less than that of the placebo treated group.  It is anticipated that the true hazard 
ratio of denosumab compared with placebo will be 0.8.  

(cid:22)(cid:17)(cid:3)

(cid:22)(cid:17)(cid:20)(cid:3)

(cid:40)(cid:59)(cid:51)(cid:40)(cid:53)(cid:44)(cid:48)(cid:40)(cid:49)(cid:55)(cid:36)(cid:47)(cid:3)(cid:51)(cid:47)(cid:36)(cid:49)(cid:3)

(cid:54)(cid:87)(cid:88)(cid:71)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:76)(cid:74)(cid:81)(cid:3)

This is an international, phase 3, randomized, double-blind, placebo-controlled study in 
subjects with hormone refractory (androgen independent) prostate cancer.  
Approximately 1400 subjects will be randomized in a 1:1 ratio to receive denosumab at a
dose of 120 mg, SC, Q4W or placebo, SC, Q4W.  

The randomization schedule will be stratified based on PSA criteria (PSA level 
(cid:116) 8.0 ng/mL AND PSA doubling time (cid:100) 10.0 months [yes/no]) and previous or current 
chemotherapy for prostate cancer (yes/no).  Subjects will receive investigational product
(IP) until the end of treatment.  The treatment period will end after approximately
660 subjects have developed bone metastasis or died and the primary efficacy and 
safety analysis is completed.

If denosumab is determined to have a positive benefit:risk profile compared with 
placebo, all subjects currently undergoing every 4 weeks scheduled assessments will be 
offered open-label denosumab at a dose of 120 mg SC until subjects have developed a 
bone metastasis, access to commercially available product in this setting, or for up to
3 years, whichever comes first.  If the benefit:risk profile is not positive, all subjects will 
be followed for survival for 3 years after the last dose of blinded IP.

The overall study design is described by a study schema at the end of the protocol 
synopsis section.

The study endpoints are defined in Section 9.2. 

(cid:22)(cid:17)(cid:21)(cid:3)

(cid:49)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:69)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:38)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:3)

Approximately 375 investigative sites will participate in this study worldwide.  Sites that 
do not enroll a subject within 6 months of site initiation may be terminated.

Participants in this clinical investigation shall be referred to as “subjects”.

Subjects who meet the eligibility criteria will be randomized to 1 of the 2 treatment 
groups.  Approximately 700 subjects will be randomized to each treatment group, for a 
total planned sample size of approximately 1400 subjects.  An anticipated 10% per year 
loss to follow-up rate has been anticipated.  Refer to Section 10.3 for details on the 
rationale for the number of subjects.

(cid:22)(cid:17)(cid:23)(cid:3)

(cid:40)(cid:86)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:87)(cid:88)(cid:71)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:88)(cid:85)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:3)

The anticipated total duration of the blinded treatment phase will be approximately 
52 months from first subject enrolled.  This represents subject recruitment, time for 
approximately 660 subjects to develop bone metastasis or died, and continued blinded 
treatment until the primary analysis is complete and the benefit:risk profile of denosumab 
is determined.  Actual study duration may be longer or shorter, depending on the time it 
takes for approximately 660 subjects to have developed bone metastasis or died.

Following the blinded treatment phase, if positive benefit:risk is determined then all 
subjects continuing with every 4 weeks scheduled assessments will be offered 
open-label denosumab.  Otherwise, subjects will be followed for survival for up to 
3 years.

The estimated time on the blinded treatment phase for an individual participant is up to
approximately 52 months, based on actual enrollment and observed attrition. The 
open-label extension or survival follow-up will be up to 3 years.  The maximum study 
participation for an individual subject will be up to approximately 88 months. Actual 
study duration may be longer or shorter, depending on the time it takes for 
approximately 660 subjects to have developed bone metastasis or died.

If the benefit:risk is positive, the end of study visit for an individual subject is defined as 4 
weeks after the last dose of denosumab in the open-label treatment phase.  If the 
benefit:risk is not positive, the end of study is defined as 4 weeks after the last dose of 
investigational product in the end of the blinded treatment phase.

For subjects ending study participation before the open-label treatment phase or ending 
treatment during the open-label treatment phase, follow up survival data will be collected 
every 6 months for up to 3 years after their last dose of blinded investigational product.   

Amgen Inc will set a primary analysis data-cut off date for the primary analysis in 
anticipation of approximately 660 subjects having developed bone metastasis or died.
Hence the analysis will be based on data from randomization through the primary 
analysis data cut-off date (ie, events occurring after the primary analysis data-cut off
date are not included in the efficacy analysis).  

The end of study is defined as the time at which the last subject completes the end of 
study visit.  Amgen Inc will also monitor the blinded, pooled-group rate of 
bone-metastases free survival pooled by treatment group; if it is lower than expected, 
Amgen Inc may choose to modify the sample size.

(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:26)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:28)(cid:23)(cid:3)

number must remain constant throughout the entire clinical study; it must not be 
changed at the time of rescreening, enrollment, or randomization.  This number will not 
necessarily be the same as the randomization number assigned for the study.  

The subject identification number will consist of 9 digits.  The first 3 digits will represent a 
protocol identifier (ie, 147) and will be identical for all sites.  The next 3 digits will 
represent the site number (eg, 101, 102, 103) and will be identical for all subjects at a 
particular site.  The last 3 digits will represent the subject identification and will be 
assigned in sequential order, per site, as subjects are screened (eg, 001, 002, 003).  
Therefore, the first subject to enter screening at site 101 will receive the number 
147101001; the second subject at this site will receive the number 147101002, etc.

Refer to Section 7 and Appendix A for screening procedures and medical history details.
Subjects may be re-screened 2 times (collection of informed consent is required for each 
screening attempt).  If a subject fails to meet all entry criteria after 3 attempts, the 
subject may not be enrolled into the study.

(cid:24)(cid:17)(cid:21)(cid:3)

(cid:55)(cid:85)(cid:72)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:76)(cid:74)(cid:81)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)

A subject who gives written informed consent and who satisfies all the inclusion and 
exclusion criteria may be randomized into the study.  Questions about subject eligibility 
should be discussed (and documented) with Amgen Inc or their designee before 
randomization.  

A subject will be randomized by IVRS after completion of all screening assessments but 
before administration of investigational product on study day 1.  Subjects will be stratified 
based on PSA criteria (PSA level (cid:116) 8.0 ng/mL AND PSA doubling time (cid:100) 10.0 months 
[yes/no]) and previous or current chemotherapy for prostate cancer (yes/no).

If unblinding is necessary, notification of treatment assignment will be by telephone with 
the central randomization center.

(cid:120)
(cid:120)

denosumab, 120 mg, SC, Q4W, or
placebo, SC, Q4W

All doses should be administered by a licensed health care professional after all other
study visit procedures have been completed, except imaging. The first dose of 
investigational product must be administered within 8 days of randomization.  

There have been no reports of overdose with this product.  It is possible that an 
overdose may result in hypocalcemia.  Hypocalcemia, if severe, should be managed by 
oral or parenteral calcium replacement, as clinically indicated.  

Refer to the pharmacy guide (Appendix B) for detailed information on the administration 
of denosumab.

If an on-study dose (eg week 5, week, 9, etc.) is delayed for more than 7 calendar days, 
it will be considered a missed dose and recorded as such on the CRFs.  The next dose 
is to be given on the next scheduled visit date (based on study day 1).  There must be at 
least a 3-week interval between administration of investigational product.

(cid:39)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:40)(cid:86)(cid:70)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:3)(cid:68)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:83)(cid:83)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:53)(cid:88)(cid:79)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:3)

There are no planned dose escalations in this study.

Administration of investigational product will be withheld for any subject who experiences 
a grade 3 or 4 adverse event (refer to CTCAE Version 3.0) reported by the investigator 
to be related to investigational product.  Re-exposure to investigational product may 
occur only when the event resolves to grade 1 or less and the investigator and sponsor 
agree subject safety will not be compromised.

Subjects will continue to receive investigational product until one of the following occurs:  
the investigator or Amgen Inc recommends discontinuation, the subject decides to
discontinue for any reason, bone metastasis develop (confirmed by central reader), or 
the study is  terminated (approximately 660 subjects have developed bone metastasis or 
died).

It is strongly recommended that all subjects receive daily supplements of at least 500 mg

serum calcium (cid:116) 2.9 mmol/L [11.5 mg/dL] or ionized calcium > 1.5 mmol/L) develops on 
study.  Due to differences in regional availability, a dosage form of vitamin D that gives 
an equivalent of 400 IU daily may be given.  Supplements will be recorded as 
concomitant medication on the CRF.  Refer to the protocol Study Guide for specific 
instructions.(cid:3)

Bisphosphonates (IV or oral) are not to be administered during the treatment period. 
Subjects who begin a bisphosphonate regimen during the treatment period will be 
withdrawn from the treatment phase of the study.  However, they should continue with 
study procedures per the Schedule of Assessment (Appendix A).  Use of any other 
investigational product (ie administered as part of another investigational trial or not 
approved for any indication by the applicable regulatory agency) is not allowed until after 
all the end of study assessments are completed.

(cid:51)(cid:54)(cid:36)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:82)(cid:88)(cid:69)(cid:79)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:55)(cid:76)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:38)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:70)(cid:88)(cid:79)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:3)

PSA doubling time is a stratification variable, therefore all subjects enrolled must have a 
calculated PSA doubling time at the time of randomization.  PSA doubling time 
(PSA-DT) will be calculated using a linear regression model.  In the model, the logarithm 
of PSA will be modeled as a linear function of time.  The PSA-DT will be calculated as 
the product of log 2 multiplied by the reciprocal of the slope of the regression equation, 
for which the logarithm is the natural log function.  The PSA doubling time formula will be 
programmed into the IVRS.  The IVRS will perform the actual PSA doubling time 
calculation.  The site staff will enter following data into the IVRS:  date of PSA value and 
actual PSA value in ng/mL.  
(cid:3)

Full body radioisotope bone scans are required for the exclusion of bone metastases at 
baseline. Radioisotope bone scans, x-rays, CT and MRI scans obtained during 
screening or within 3 months before randomization, will be analyzed by the central 
imaging vendor to determine subject eligibility. 

Eligibility assessment by central imaging vendor: 

(cid:120)

(cid:120)

(cid:120)

If the baseline radioisotope bone scan and skeletal survey (x-rays) are normal, the 
subject is eligible. 
If the baseline radioisotope bone scan is abnormal but not suggestive of bone 
metastases and the baseline skeletal survey (x-rays) or additional imaging (ie, CT or 
MRI scans initiated by investigator or the central imaging vendor) excludes bone 
metastasis (ie benign pathology determined), the subject is eligible. 
If the baseline radioisotope bone scan is highly suggestive of metastases, no further 
testing should be performed and the subject should be screen failed.

(cid:57)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:85)(cid:68)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:88)(cid:85)(cid:72)(cid:3)

During the blinded treatment phase, vertebral fractures will be identified by visual 
inspection by an expert radiologist (at the central imaging vendor).   

For assessment of vertebral fractures (vertebrae T4 to L4), a generally accepted 
semiquantitative grading scale will be used (Genant et al, 1993): Grade 0, normal; 
Grade 1, 20 to 25% reduction in vertebral height (anterior, middle, or posterior); Grade 2, 
25 to 40% reduction in height; Grade 3, greater than 40% reduction in height.  Vertebral 
fracture is defined as a vertebrum with a semiquantitative grade of greater than or equal 
to 1.  

If the investigator suspects a vertebral fracture, a radiograph is to be obtained. During 
the blinded treatment phase, radiographs will be submitted to the central imaging vendor 
for confirmation of fracture.

During the open-label treatment phase, vertebral fractures identified by the site will be 
recorded on the case report form.

(cid:26)(cid:17)(cid:20)(cid:21)(cid:3)

(cid:49)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:16)(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:85)(cid:68)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:88)(cid:85)(cid:72)(cid:3)

Any new non-vertebral fractures while on study will be recorded.  During the blinded 
treatment phase, radiographs confirming the fracture, as well as a copy of the 
radiologist’s report, should be obtained and included in the subject’s study records.  
During the blinded treatment phase, radiographs will be submitted to the central imaging 
vendor for confirmation of fracture.

During the open-label treatment phase, non-vertebral fractures identified by the site will 
be recorded on the case report form.

The central laboratory will be responsible for all screening and on-study serum

(cid:26)(cid:17)(cid:20)(cid:22)(cid:17)(cid:20)(cid:3)

(cid:37)(cid:79)(cid:82)(cid:82)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:68)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:86)(cid:3)

All blood samples will be obtained by venipuncture before investigational product 
administration.  The total volume of blood drawn from a subject throughout the study 
(based on an average estimated treatment period of 27 months) will be approximately 
250 mL, including screening.  

Blood will be obtained for the following assessments at the time points outlined in 
Appendix A. Table 2 outlines the specific analytes for each assessment.  The date and 
time of blood collection will be recorded in the subjects’ medical records.  

To maintain the integrity of the study blind, Week 5 and Week 9 laboratory results for 
calcium (or albumin-adjusted calcium if applicable) and phosphorus will not be reported 
to the sites.  To ensure adequate safety oversight, if there is a change of these analytes 
to CTCAE grade 3 or greater, the central laboratory will notify both the investigative site 
and Amgen Inc of the absolute analyte value.  All on-study alkaline phosphatase results 
will be blinded to the sites.  

Serum denosumab trough levels will be obtained on a subset of 150 subjects prior to 
administration of the investigational products on Study Day 1, Week 5, Week 9, 
Week 13, Week 25, Week 49, Week 73 and the end of study visit. The centers that will 
participate in this part of the study, as well as the number of subjects per center, will be 
determined at the time of site selection, on the basis of center interest and recruitment 
capacity.

(cid:56)(cid:85)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:86)(cid:3)

Urine samples will be collected for the urinary N-telopeptide (uNTx) assay and alpha 
CTX assay.   

A morning urine sample (after the first morning void, before noon) must be collected.  It 
is recommended that urine samples be collected in the clinic, if feasible.

If the subject is to collect the urine sample at home, he will need to be provided with 
containers for sample collection and for transporting the sample to the site on the day of 
collection.  Subject instructions will be provided on how and when to collect the sample, 
recording the time of collection, and storing the sample (refrigerated) until it is brought to 
the study site for processing.  

Urine analytes will include creatinine, raw N-telopeptide (NTx), and NTx corrected for 
urine creatinine.

(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:71)(cid:88)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:69)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:36)(cid:48)(cid:42)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:25)(cid:21)(cid:12)(cid:3)

(cid:39)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:88)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:22)(cid:27)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:28)(cid:23)(cid:3)

The uNTx will be corrected for urine creatinine by generating a ratio.  Using the uNTx as 
reported in units of nM and urine creatinine in units of mg/dL, the creatinine 
measurement will be multiplied by 0.0884, and used to generate the corrected ratio.  The 
resulting equation will be:

uNTx/Cr (nM BCE/mM) = uNTx/(Cr*0.0884)

(cid:26)(cid:17)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:53)(cid:50)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:86)(cid:3)

PRO assessments should be completed before any other study procedures at each 
study visit as noted in the Schedule of Assessments (Appendix A).  Three validated tools 
will be used including BPI-SF, FACT-P, and EQ-5D.

(cid:26)(cid:17)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:17)(cid:20)(cid:3)

(cid:37)(cid:85)(cid:76)(cid:72)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:3)(cid:44)(cid:81)(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:177)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:75)(cid:82)(cid:85)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:82)(cid:85)(cid:80)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:37)(cid:51)(cid:44)(cid:16)(cid:54)(cid:41)(cid:12)(cid:3)

The BPI-SF is a questionnaire specifically designed to assess pain in cancer.  The 
BPI-SF captures information on the intensity of pain (pain severity) as well as the degree 
to which pain interferes with function (pain interference).  The questionnaire is comprised 
of 8 items, which are exploratory endpoints in this study.  Evidence for reliability and 
validity of the BPI-SF has been well documented in cancer patients (Cleeland CS, 1991).  
See Appendix D for questionnaire.

(cid:26)(cid:17)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:17)(cid:21)(cid:3)

(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:88)(cid:81)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:38)(cid:68)(cid:81)(cid:70)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:3)(cid:55)(cid:75)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:68)(cid:83)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:177)(cid:3)(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:87)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:38)(cid:68)(cid:81)(cid:70)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:3)
(cid:11)(cid:41)(cid:36)(cid:38)(cid:55)(cid:16)(cid:51)(cid:12)(cid:3)

The FACT-G is a widely used disease specific health-related quality of life (HRQOL) 
instrument that has been shown to be valid and reliable in patients with cancer.  It was 
developed in 1993 (Cella et al, 1993) and is comprised of 27 questions evaluating the 
HRQOL domains of physical well being, functional well being, social/family well being, 
and emotional well being in patients with cancer.  An additional scale with 12 questions 
specific to prostate cancer was developed in 1997 (Esper et al, 1997) which addresses 
concerns of prostate cancer patients.  All 39 questions administered together have been
termed the FACT-P and this instrument has been validated in men with prostate cancer.  
See Appendix E for the questionnaire.  

(cid:26)(cid:17)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:17)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:40)(cid:88)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:52)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:16)(cid:24)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:76)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:86)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:40)(cid:52)(cid:16)(cid:24)(cid:39)(cid:12)(cid:3)

The EQ-5D, developed in 1990, is a widely used generic HRQOL instrument that allows 
for estimation of Quality Adjusted Life Years (QALY), a requirement for reimbursement 
dossiers and formulary submissions.  The EQ-5D is comprised of 6 questions.  The first 

(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:71)(cid:88)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:69)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:36)(cid:48)(cid:42)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:25)(cid:21)(cid:12)(cid:3)
(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:49)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:69)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:19)(cid:24)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:26)(cid:3)(cid:177)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:88)(cid:83)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:23)(cid:3)
(cid:39)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:88)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:22)(cid:28)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:28)(cid:23)(cid:3)

5 questions address the following quality of life dimensions: mobility, self-care, usual 
activities, pain/discomfort and anxiety /depression.  Each of these questions has a 
simple three-category response scale.  The last question is represented by a 20-cm 
vertical Visual Analogue Scale (VAS), scored from 0 to 100 asking the patient to “mark 
your own health state today” (Brooks, 1996).  See Appendix F for questionnaire.

Subjects who withdraw early from investigational product during the blinded-treatment 
phase will continue on study, without investigational product administration, per the 
Schedule of Assessment as specified in Appendix A.

Subjects who withdraw from investigational product during the open-label treatment 
phase will have an end of study visit approximately 4 weeks after the last dose of 
investigational product. These subjects will have follow up survival data collected every 
6 months for up to 3 years after their last dose of blinded investigational product.

For subjects ending study participation before the open-label treatment phase or ending 
treatment during the open-label treatment phase, follow-up survival information will be 
collected by clinic visit or telephone contact every 6 months for up to 3 years after the 
last dose of blinded IP.  At the first follow-up visit only (6 months (cid:114) 2 weeks from the End 
of Study date), a blood sample will be obtained for denosumab antibody assessment.

any reason without prejudice to his future medical care by the physician or at the

Withdrawal of full consent for a study means that the subject does not wish to receive 
further investigational treatment and does not wish to or is unable to continue further 
study participation.  Any subject may withdraw full consent to participate in the study at 
any time during the study.  The investigator will discuss with the subject the most 
appropriate way to withdraw to ensure the subject’s health.  

Withdrawal of partial consent means that the subject does not wish to take 
investigational product any longer but is still willing to collaborate in providing further 
data by continuing on study (eg, participate in all subsequent study visits or procedures).
Subjects may decline to continue receiving investigational product at any time during the 
study.  These subjects, as well as those who have stopped receiving investigational 
product for other reasons (eg, investigator or sponsor concern) should continue the 
schedule of study observations.  

Reasons for removal from investigational product or observation might include:

(cid:120) withdrawal of consent

An adverse event is defined as an undesirable medical occurrence (eg, sign, symptom, 
or diagnosis) or worsening of a pre-existing medical condition.

Worsening of a pre-existing medical condition is when a condition (eg, diabetes, 
migraine headaches, gout) becomes more severe, more frequent, longer in duration, or 
associated with significantly worse outcomes. 

Prostate cancer disease progression should not be recorded as an adverse event.

(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:71)(cid:88)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:69)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:36)(cid:48)(cid:42)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:25)(cid:21)(cid:12)(cid:3)
(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:49)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:69)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:19)(cid:24)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:26)(cid:3)(cid:177)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:88)(cid:83)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:23)(cid:3)
(cid:39)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:88)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:23)(cid:20)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:28)(cid:23)(cid:3)

Interventions for pretreatment conditions (eg, elective cosmetic surgery) or medical 
procedures that were planned before study enrollment are not considered adverse 
events.  

All of the following are considered adverse events and are to be recorded:

(cid:120) Adverse events that occur after signing of the informed consent form are recorded as 

protocol-associated adverse events.

(cid:120) Adverse events occurring after exposure to investigational product are recorded as 
study-associated adverse events, or procedure-related, depending on investigator 
evaluation. 

(cid:120) Adverse events deemed potentially related, in the opinion of the investigator, to 

investigational product are recorded as study-related adverse events.

(cid:120) Adverse events deemed potentially related, in the opinion of the investigator, to 

protocol procedures are recorded as protocol-related adverse events.

The investigator is responsible for reviewing laboratory test results and determining 
whether an abnormal value in an individual study subject represents a change from 
values before the study.  In general, abnormal laboratory findings without clinical 
significance (based on the investigator's judgment) should not be recorded as adverse 
events; however, laboratory value changes requiring therapy or adjustment in prior 
therapy are considered adverse events.

A serious adverse event (SAE) is defined (cid:68)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:68)(cid:81)(cid:3)(cid:68)(cid:71)(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:72)(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:87)(cid:75)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:72)(cid:87)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:79)(cid:72)(cid:68)(cid:86)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)
(cid:87)(cid:75)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:73)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:79)(cid:82)(cid:90)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:88)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:70)(cid:85)(cid:76)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:76)(cid:68)(cid:29)

(cid:120)

(cid:120)
(cid:120)
(cid:120)

is fatal
is life threatening (places the subject at immediate risk of death)
requires in-patient hospitalization or prolongation of existing hospitalization
results in persistent or significant disability/incapacity
is a congenital anomaly/birth defect
other significant medical hazard

A hospitalization meeting the regulatory definition for “serious” is any inpatient hospital 
admission that includes a minimum of an overnight stay in a health care facility excluding 
hospitalizations for anticipated protocol-specified procedures, or administration of 
radiotherapy, chemotherapy, or blood product transfusions, if being administered for 
cancer-related treatment.  However, prolongation of hospitalization or re-admission after 
the subject has been discharged would be considered a Serious Adverse Event.

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:71)(cid:88)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:69)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:36)(cid:48)(cid:42)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:25)(cid:21)(cid:12)(cid:3)
(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:49)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:69)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:19)(cid:24)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:23)(cid:26)(cid:3)(cid:177)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:88)(cid:83)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:23)(cid:3)
(cid:39)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:29)(cid:3)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:41)(cid:72)(cid:69)(cid:85)(cid:88)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:21)(cid:19)(cid:20)(cid:22)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:23)(cid:21)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:28)(cid:23)(cid:3)

Any adverse event that does not meet one of the definitions of serious (eg, emergency 
room visit, outpatient surgery, or requires urgent investigation) may be considered by the 
investigator to meet the “other significant medical hazard” criterion for classification as a 
serious adverse event.  Examples include allergic bronchospasm, convulsions, and 
blood dyscrasias. 

(cid:28)(cid:17)(cid:21)(cid:3)

(cid:53)(cid:72)(cid:83)(cid:82)(cid:85)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:88)(cid:85)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:73)(cid:82)(cid:85)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:79)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:71)(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:40)(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:86)(cid:3)

Adverse events will be collected beginning with the signing of the informed consent 
through 30 days after the last dose of investigational product.

The investigator is responsible for ensuring that all adverse events (as defined in 
Section 9.1) observed by the investigator or reported by subjects are properly recorded 
in designated study documents.  In addition, the investigator is responsible for ensuring 
that all adverse events are properly recorded in the subjects’ records.

The following adverse event attributes must be assigned by the investigator:  event 
description; dates of onset and resolution; severity; assessment of relatedness to 
investigational product; and action taken.  Diagnoses or syndromes—rather than signs 
or symptoms—should be recorded.  The investigator may be asked to provide follow-up
information, discharge summaries, and extracts from medical records or CRFs.

The relationship of the adverse event to the investigational product will be assessed by 
means of the question:  “Is there a reasonable possibility that the event may have been 
caused by the investigational product?”  The investigator should respond to this question 
with either yes or no.

Severity grading scales are described in Appendix G.

Medically significant adverse events considered related to the investigational product by 
the investigator or the sponsor will be followed until resolved or considered stable.

It will be left to the investigator’s clinical judgment to determine whether an adverse 
event is related and of sufficient severity to require the subject’s removal from treatment.  
A subject may also voluntarily withdraw from treatment due to what he or she perceives 
as an intolerable adverse event.  If either of these situations arises, the subject must 
undergo an end-of-study assessment and be under medical supervision until symptoms 
cease or the condition becomes stable.

Serious adverse events will be collected beginning with the signing of the informed 
consent through 30 days after the last dose of investigational product. 

All serious adverse events must be reported to Amgen Inc within (cid:21)(cid:23)(cid:3)(cid:75)(cid:82)(cid:88)(cid:85)(cid:86) of discovery 
or notification of the event.  Initial serious adverse event information and all amendments 
or additions must be recorded on a Serious Adverse Event Report form (see 
Appendix H) and faxed to Amgen Global Safety.

For all deaths, available autopsy reports and relevant medical reports should be faxed to 
Amgen Global Safety.  For this reporting process, subject assessments must be made 
30 days or longer after administration of the last dose of investigational product.  

If a subject is permanently withdrawn from the study because of a serious adverse 
event, this information must be included in the initial or follow-up Serious Adverse Event 
Report Form as well as the End of Study Case Report Form.(cid:3)

To comply with worldwide serious adverse event reporting regulations, the treatment 
assignment of subjects who develop serious, unexpected, and related adverse events 
will be unblinded before submission to regulatory authorities.  (cid:44)(cid:81)(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:74)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:90)(cid:76)(cid:79)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:85)(cid:72)(cid:70)(cid:72)(cid:76)(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:3)

(cid:54)(cid:55)(cid:36)(cid:55)(cid:44)(cid:54)(cid:55)(cid:44)(cid:38)(cid:36)(cid:47)(cid:3)(cid:38)(cid:50)(cid:49)(cid:54)(cid:44)(cid:39)(cid:40)(cid:53)(cid:36)(cid:55)(cid:44)(cid:50)(cid:49)(cid:54)(cid:3)

(cid:54)(cid:87)(cid:88)(cid:71)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:76)(cid:74)(cid:81)(cid:3)

This is an international, phase 3, randomized, double blind, placebo-controlled study in 
subjects with hormone refractory (androgen independent) prostate cancer.  
Approximately 1400 subjects will be randomly assigned to receive denosumab or 
placebo in 1:1 allocation ratio.  The randomization schedule will be stratified based on 
PSA criteria (PSA level (cid:116) 8.0 ng/mL AND PSA doubling time (cid:100) 10.0 months [yes/no]) 
and previous or current chemotherapy for prostate cancer (yes/no).  The treatment 
period will end after approximately 660 subjects have developed bone metastasis or 
died and the primary efficacy and safety analysis is completed.

If denosumab is determined to have a positive benefit:risk profile compared with 
placebo, all subjects currently undergoing every 4 weeks scheduled assessments will be 
offered open-label denosumab at a dose of 120 mg SC until subjects have developed a 
bone metastasis, access to commercially available product in this setting, or for up to 
3 years, whichever comes first.  If the benefit:risk profile is not positive, all subjects will 
be followed for survival for 3 years after the last dose of blinded IP.

Details are provided in Section 3.1

The principal analysis for the primary endpoint and secondary endpoints will employ the 
full analysis set (FAS) approach; the per-protocol approach will be considered 
supportive.  The FAS subject set is defined as all subjects who are randomized to the 
study.  The safety analysis subset will include all randomized subjects who received at 
least 1 dose of investigational product.  The per-protocol subset is defined as all subjects 
with a protocol-defined diagnosis, no major protocol violations, and who received at least 
1 dose of investigational product.  The major protocol violations will be defined in the 
Statistical Analysis Plan (SAP).

(cid:54)(cid:68)(cid:80)(cid:83)(cid:79)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:76)(cid:93)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:38)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:86)(cid:76)(cid:71)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:86)(cid:3)

Approximately 1400 subjects will be enrolled into this trial and it will conclude when 
approximately 660 subjects have developed bone metastasis or died.  Assuming the 
hazard ratio of denosumab versus placebo is 0.8, this number of study events will 
provide approximately 80% power at a significance level of 0.025 using a 1 sided 
maximum likelihood test.  One interim analysis will be conducted when approximately 
330 events of bone metastasis or death have occurred.  The interim analysis will allow 
for early rejection of the null hypothesis or the alternative hypothesis, with critical 
p-values determined by the Lan-DeMets spending function with an O’Brien-Fleming 
approach.  Assuming an enrollment period of 15 months, approximately 93 subjects per 
month enrolled, median time to bone metastasis or death of 26.5 months for the placebo 
group (Smith et al, 2005) and a lost to follow-up rate of 10% per year, the maximum 
study duration is approximately 42 months.  As of this amendment, the study duration is 
expected to be 52 months due to different enrollment rate, event rate, and dropout rate 
than originally expected.

Amgen Inc will also monitor the rate of bone-metastases survival pooled by treatment 
group; if it is lower than expected, Amgen Inc may choose to modify the sample size.  

(cid:20)(cid:19)(cid:17)(cid:23)(cid:3)

(cid:36)(cid:70)(cid:70)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:3)(cid:44)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:76)(cid:89)(cid:76)(cid:71)(cid:88)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:88)(cid:69)(cid:77)(cid:72)(cid:70)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:55)(cid:85)(cid:72)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:76)(cid:74)(cid:81)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:86)(cid:3)

This is a double-blinded study.  Subject treatment assignments will remain blinded to 
investigators, subjects and Amgen Inc in order to reduce bias.  The external DMC will 
have access to subject treatment assignments. To minimize the potential introduction of 
bias, these individuals will not have any direct contact with the study site personnel or 
subjects. 

The identity of investigational product assigned to subjects or to individual boxes of 
investigational product will be contained in the IVRS.  Authorized site staff will be 
provided with a unique Personal Identification Number (PIN) to access the IVRS to

obtain unblinding information.  This PIN is unique to the individual and must not be 
shared.

A subject’s treatment assignment should only be unblinded when knowledge of the 
treatment is essential for the further management of the subject.  Unblinding at the study 
site for any other reason will be considered a protocol deviation.  The principal 
investigator is strongly encouraged to contact the key study contact before unblinding 
any subject’s treatment assignment, but must do so within 1 working day after the event 
and must document the unblinding in the subject’s case report form.  

(cid:20)(cid:19)(cid:17)(cid:24)(cid:3)

(cid:44)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:76)(cid:80)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:81)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:92)(cid:86)(cid:76)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:68)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:40)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:79)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:83)(cid:83)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:42)(cid:88)(cid:76)(cid:71)(cid:72)(cid:79)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:3)

An external DMC will be formed with members consisting of individuals chosen for their 
expertise in oncology.  The role of this external DMC will be to monitor safety and 
efficacy at regular intervals.  Selected Amgen Inc staff may serve as liaisons to the 
external DMC, but will not be voting members, and will not be unblinded to the results.  
The DMC will have access to subject’s individual treatment assignments. To minimize 
the potential introduction of bias, these individuals will not have any direct contact with 
the study site personnel or subjects. Members of this external DMC will include, at a 
minimum, physicians external to Amgen Inc, and appropriate statistical representation 
external to Amgen Inc. Unblinded reports of safety data for review will be generated by 
entities that are external to Amgen Inc as well.  

This external DMC will convene approximately twice yearly, and the start date will 
depend on subject accrual rates.
It is recognized that the DMC may feel ethically
compelled to recommend early stopping in the event of overwhelming efficacy. The
stopping rules are defined as follows: 

1. There is one formal interim analysis when approximately 330 events of bone 

metastasis or death have occurred.  The critical p-values for rejecting the null and 
alternative hypothesis, as determined by Lan-DeMets spending function with an 
O’Brien-Fleming approach, are listed in Table 3. 

2. At other interim evaluations, the DMC will focus on safety, and will review efficacy 

data only to balance the risk-benefit assessment.  At these analyses, the guideline is 
that a p-value for the primary efficacy analysis of less than 0.0005 will be used as 
evidence of overwhelming efficacy to stop the study.

Amgen will set a primary analysis data cut-off date in anticipation of 660 subjects having 
developed bone metastasis or died. The analysis will be based on the data from 
randomization through the primary analysis data cut-off date.

The principal analysis for the primary endpoint will employ the FAS and the per-protocol 
approach will be considered supportive.  Safety analyses will be performed using the 
FAS subjects who received at least 1 dose of investigational product.  

Subjects who withdraw from investigational product early will be followed for the 
development of the primary and secondary endpoints whenever possible.  Subjects 
completing the study and not experiencing an event will be censored regardless of 
compliance with study therapy.

If denosumab is determined to be superior to placebo with respect to the primary 
efficacy endpoint at a corresponding level listed in Table 3 (above), then the secondary 
endpoint time to first bone metastasis (either symptomatic or asymptomatic) excluding 
death will be tested for superiority at a 1-sided significance level of 0.025.  If denosumab 
is further determined to be superior to placebo with respect to time to first bone 
metastasis (either symptomatic or asymptomatic) excluding death, then the secondary 
endpoint overall survival time will be tested for superiority at a 1-sided significance level 
of 0.025.

(cid:36)(cid:81)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:92)(cid:86)(cid:76)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:46)(cid:72)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:87)(cid:88)(cid:71)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:40)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:83)(cid:82)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:86)(cid:3)

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:76)(cid:80)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:40)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:83)(cid:82)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)

For bone metastasis-free survival, Kaplan-Meier estimates (Kaplan et al, 1958) will be 
graphically displayed and a Cox proportional hazard model (Cox, 1972) with treatment 
groups as the independent variable and stratified by the randomization stratification 
factors will be used.  A supportive analysis will use a Cox model to evaluate the 
covariates that may modify the outcome.  The hazard ratio of denosumab compared with 
placebo and its corresponding 2-sided confidence interval will be estimated, and p-value 
for the superiority test will be provided.

(cid:54)(cid:72)(cid:70)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:68)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:40)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:83)(cid:82)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:86)(cid:3)

For the following endpoints: time to first bone metastasis (either symptomatic or 
asymptomatic) excluding deaths, and overall survival time, a similar approach as for the 
primary endpoint will be used.

(cid:54)(cid:68)(cid:73)(cid:72)(cid:87)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:81)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:92)(cid:86)(cid:76)(cid:86)(cid:3)

(cid:36)(cid:71)(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:40)(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:86)(cid:3)

Safety data will be summarized for all randomized patients who receive at least 1 dose
of investigational products.  All AEs will be coded using the Medical Dictionary for 
Regulatory Activities (MedDRA).  An adverse event will be analyzed as treatment 
emergent if the indicator of “Did event start before the first dose of investigational 
product?” is checked as “No” on Adverse Events Summary CRF pages.  Based on the 
AEs summary instructions, an AE that exists prior to the administration of IP and gets 
worse after the first dose of IP will be included as a treatment emergent adverse event.

The primary analysis of adverse events will be descriptive. The subject incidence rates 
and adjusted adverse event rate of treatment-emergent AEs reported through the 
primary analysis data cut-off date during the study period will be tabulated by system
organ class and preferred term. Additional summary tables will include the adjusted 
adverse event rates and subject incidence rates tabulated separately for serious AEs, 
Common Terminology Criteria for Adverse Events (CTCAE) grade 3, 4 or 5 AEs, AEs 
leading to IP discontinuation, and AEs leading to study withdrawal.  Narratives of deaths 
and serious AEs will also be provided.  All IP related AEs, Serious AEs, CTCAE grade 3, 
4 or 5 AEs, AEs leading to IP discontinuation, and AEs leading to study withdrawal will 
be summarized in the same manner as treatment-emergent AEs.  All AEs, CTCAE 
grade 3, 4, or 5 AEs, and SAEs will also be examined by the subgroups of age and race.

Laboratory parameters will be summarized over time using shifts in recorded values 
from baseline to “worst” on-study value and from baseline to a particular visit.  Graphical 
representations of aggregate data may also be presented.  Continuously distributed 
analytes will be summarized descriptively using the number of non-missing 
observations, mean, median, standard deviation, standard error, minimum, and 
maximum.  Frequencies and percentages will be presented for categorical variables.

Denosumab will be presented as a sterile, colorless to slightly yellow, practically free 
from particles, preservative free liquid in blinded-label glass vials.  The formulation is 
60 mg denosumab per mL of 10 mM Sodium Acetate, 5% sorbitol, with a pH of 5.2 for 
the blinded treatment phase. Placebo will be presented in matched containers and the 
formulation will be identical to denosumab with the exception of the protein content. For 
the open-label extension phase, the formulation is 60 mg denosumab per mL of 10 mM 
Sodium Acetate, 5% sorbitol, with a pH of 5.2(cid:3)or 70 mg per mL denosumab, 18 mM 
acetate and 4.6% sorbitol at a pH of 5.2.

The box number of investigational product is to be recorded on each subject’s 
investigational product administration CRF.  

Unique boxes will be assigned for each dose the subject will receive while on study.  To 
obtain box number assignment for a schedule dose, site personnel should call the IVRS.  

Refer to Sections 10.4 for conditions and requirements for unblinding. 

Investigational product details for denosumab including labeling, storage, preparation, 
etc., are provided in the Pharmacy Guide, Appendix B.

(cid:20)(cid:20)(cid:17)(cid:21)(cid:3)

(cid:36)(cid:70)(cid:70)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:3)(cid:55)(cid:85)(cid:72)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:76)(cid:74)(cid:81)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:86)(cid:3)

The identity of investigational product assigned to subject numbers or to individual boxes 
of investigational product will be available for emergency situations through an IVRS.  
Authorized site staff will be provided with a unique Personal Identification Number (PIN) 
to access the IVRS to obtain unblinding information.  This PIN is unique to the individual 
and must not be shared. 

A subject’s treatment assignment should only be unblinded when knowledge of the 
treatment is essential for the further management of the subject.  Unblinding at the study 
site for any other reason will be considered a protocol deviation.

An initial generic informed consent form has been provided to the investigator to prepare 
the informed consent document to be used at his or her site.  Updates to the template 
will be communicated by letter from the clinical study manager to the investigator.  The 
written informed consent document should be prepared in the language(s) of the 
potential patient population.

Before a subject’s participation in the clinical study, the investigator is responsible for 
obtaining written informed consent from the subject or legally acceptable representative 
(see note below) after adequate explanation of the aims, methods, anticipated benefits, 
and potential hazards of the study and before any protocol-specific screening 
procedures or any investigational products are administered.  A legally acceptable 
representative is an individual or other body authorized under applicable law to consent, 
on behalf of a prospective subject, to the subject’s participation in the clinical study.  

The investigator is also responsible for asking the subject if the subject agrees to have 
his/her primary care physician informed of the subject’s participation in the clinical study.  
If the subject agrees to such notification, the investigator shall inform the subject’s 
primary care physician of the subject’s participation in the clinical study.

The acquisition of informed consent and the subject’s agreement or refusal of his/her 
notification of the primary care physician should be documented in the subject’s medical 
records, and the informed consent form should be signed and personally dated by the 
subject or a legally acceptable representative and by the person who conducted the

A copy of the protocol, proposed informed consent form, other written subject

document.  The investigator should notify the IEC/IRB of deviations from the protocol or

from Amgen Inc, in accordance with local procedures.

throughout the duration of the study.  Copies of the investigator’s reports and the 
IEC/IRB’s continuance of approval must be sent to Amgen Inc.

The investigator must ensure that the subject’s confidentiality is maintained.  On the 
case report forms or other documents submitted to Amgen Inc, subjects should be 
identified by subject study number only.  Documents that are not for submission to 
Amgen Inc (eg, signed informed consent forms) should be kept in strict confidence by 
the investigator.

In compliance with Federal regulations/ICH GCP Guidelines, it is required that the 
investigator and institution permit authorized representatives of the company, of the 
regulatory agency(s), and the IEC/IRB direct access to review the subject’s original 
medical records for verification of study-related procedures and data.  Direct access 
includes examining, analyzing, verifying, and reproducing any records and reports that 
are important to the evaluation of the study.  The investigator is obligated to inform and 
obtain the consent of the subject to permit named representatives to have access to his 
study-related records without violating the confidentiality of the subject.

an investigator contributing a high number of eligible subjects

(cid:51)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:82)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:68)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:54)(cid:87)(cid:88)(cid:71)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:55)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:80)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:3)

Protocol amendments, except where necessary to eliminate an immediate hazard to 
subjects, must be made only with the prior approval of Amgen Inc.  Agreement from the 
investigator must be obtained for all protocol amendments and amendments to the 
informed consent document.  The IEC/IRB must be informed of all amendments and 
give approval.  The investigator must send a copy of the approval letter from the IEC/IRB
to Amgen Inc. 

Both Amgen Inc and the investigator reserve the right to terminate the study according to 
the study contract.  The investigator should notify the IEC/IRB in writing of the study’s 
completion or early termination and send a copy of the notification to Amgen Inc. 

Subjects may be eligible for continued treatment with investigational product by 
extension protocol or as provided for by the local country’s regulatory mechanism.  
However, Amgen Inc reserves the unilateral right, at its sole discretion, to determine 
whether to supply the investigational product, and by what mechanism, after termination
of the trial and before it is available commercially.

(cid:54)(cid:87)(cid:88)(cid:71)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:39)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:88)(cid:80)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:3)(cid:68)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:85)(cid:70)(cid:75)(cid:76)(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:3)

The investigator should maintain a list of appropriately qualified persons to whom he/she 
has delegated study duties.  All persons authorized to make entries and/or corrections 
on case report forms will be included on the Amgen Inc Delegation of Authority Form.

Source documents are original documents, data, and records from which the subject’s 
case report form data are obtained.  These include but are not limited to hospital 
records, clinical and office charts, laboratory and pharmacy records, diaries, microfiches, 
radiographs, and correspondence.
